    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7755824794793171082">In this humorously irreverent take on zombies, Ax Handel is a present-day nineteen-year-old pizza delivery guy with a short fuse who is determined to take control of his wildly unpredictable life. His comical attempts to make sense of his relationships with his outrageous family members usually end up in disaster. Suddenly, his life changes—possibly for the better—when zom</span>
  <span id="freeText7755824794793171082" style="display:none">In this humorously irreverent take on zombies, Ax Handel is a present-day nineteen-year-old pizza delivery guy with a short fuse who is determined to take control of his wildly unpredictable life. His comical attempts to make sense of his relationships with his outrageous family members usually end up in disaster. Suddenly, his life changes—possibly for the better—when zombies stumble out of a nearby cemetery. Life has never been easy for Ax and his mother, and they refuse to be scared off by a horde of the dying impaired. Without any help from Ma, whose hard-living, heavy-metal past has left her strangely sympathetic to the plight of the zombies, or his volatile ex-girlfriend, Zenobia, who's certain he's a head case, or even his zoned-out fugitive father, it’s up to Ax to protect his little town of Karbunkle and what little he owns, while getting revenge on some bad-mannered, lumbering stiffs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7755824794793171082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_975709331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975709331" />
    <a title="Richard Lanson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32509907-richard-lanson"><img alt="Richard Lanson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408654290p2/32509907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975709331?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Lanson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Lanson" href="/user/show/32509907-richard-lanson">Richard Lanson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975709331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11748742624672159555">I’ve read several humorous zombie books, but this may be the best. Most refreshing is how the author amusingly chooses to ignore some of the widely held conventions regarding zombies, and to his credit makes it very funny. I love how Smith’s characters are down to earth and easy to relate to. And when they're faced with a zombie epidemic none of them seem to panic but simply take it in stride and roll with it, especially Ax Handel, the main character, who hilariously enough seems in his element.</span>
  <span id="freeText11748742624672159555" style="display:none">I’ve read several humorous zombie books, but this may be the best. Most refreshing is how the author amusingly chooses to ignore some of the widely held conventions regarding zombies, and to his credit makes it very funny. I love how Smith’s characters are down to earth and easy to relate to. And when they're faced with a zombie epidemic none of them seem to panic but simply take it in stride and roll with it, especially Ax Handel, the main character, who hilariously enough seems in his element. I’ll tell you this much: if I had zombies in my yard I’d feel a lot safer with Ax Handel around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11748742624672159555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_972093214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972093214" />
    <a title="Nathan Hennessy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32408614-nathan-hennessy"><img alt="Nathan Hennessy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408747696p2/32408614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/972093214?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan Hennessy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan Hennessy" href="/user/show/32408614-nathan-hennessy">Nathan Hennessy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer972093214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11967413324227077154">I instantly fell in love with this book. The characters are engaging and completely mental. Funniest thing I’ve read in a long time. <br/><br/>Ax Handel is not your typical hero, or typical anything. He’s a guy trying to make a buck while his world crumbles. When his girlfriend leaves him and aggravating zombies try to eat him, he does the thing we like to think we’d all do if we were in his shoes: put on a grin and kick ass. <br/><br/>Smith challenges the notion that all zombies are alike, and makes a believer out</span>
  <span id="freeText11967413324227077154" style="display:none">I instantly fell in love with this book. The characters are engaging and completely mental. Funniest thing I’ve read in a long time. <br /><br />Ax Handel is not your typical hero, or typical anything. He’s a guy trying to make a buck while his world crumbles. When his girlfriend leaves him and aggravating zombies try to eat him, he does the thing we like to think we’d all do if we were in his shoes: put on a grin and kick ass. <br /><br />Smith challenges the notion that all zombies are alike, and makes a believer out of you while making you laugh till your ribs ache.</span>

<div id="review_1016631406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1016631406" />
    <a title="Julie Robiedoux" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32672673-julie-robiedoux"><img alt="Julie Robiedoux" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016631406?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Robiedoux" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Robiedoux" href="/user/show/32672673-julie-robiedoux">Julie Robiedoux</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016631406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5756598425543440676">This is a very funny book about zombies, but what made me laugh the most were the delightfully humorous exchanges between the main character (Axel) and his estranged, caustic girlfriend, Zenobia. Her bitterness nearly drips off the page, and when Ax playfully provokes her it brings out the worst—and funniest—in her. <br/><br/>I don’t know which of Axel’s associations is more dangerous, the one with Zenobia or the one with the zombies. His relationship with his girlfriend is already dangerously strained, b</span>
  <span id="freeText5756598425543440676" style="display:none">This is a very funny book about zombies, but what made me laugh the most were the delightfully humorous exchanges between the main character (Axel) and his estranged, caustic girlfriend, Zenobia. Her bitterness nearly drips off the page, and when Ax playfully provokes her it brings out the worst—and funniest—in her. <br /><br />I don’t know which of Axel’s associations is more dangerous, the one with Zenobia or the one with the zombies. His relationship with his girlfriend is already dangerously strained, but (thankfully) she has no filters, and her devilishly biting sarcasm is hysterical and left me wanting more. Those two need therapy! Axel’s awkward nervousness around her, along with his explosive intolerance of the zombies, results in many uproarious moments throughout this book. <br /><br />Worth reading—twice! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5756598425543440676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1562739171112024303" style="display:none">If you want to laugh, pick up this book. <br /><br />The story is told by Ax Handel, a nineteen-year-old with no pretentions or excuses for not having all the answers—or using the “write” words to tell his tale. He simply goes about his business—the business of taking his yard back from zombies while trying to benefit from it. Along the way he takes a ton of grief from his mother and ex-girlfriend, who do their best to keep Ax Handel in check, as if that’s even possible. <br /><br />Funniest is his father, who has a hard time staying focused and is seemingly constantly on the run from a plethora of unknown pursuers. <br /><br />I couldn’t get enough of the descriptive action scenes where Ax fights the zombies...his emotions are hysterical!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anybody having a bad day &amp; needing a chuckle</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Loyd by: </span>
      Colleague
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096669876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17311132156897922260">There are a lot of zombie books out there, but maybe none as funny as this one. Best of all, it’s uniquely refreshing in its irreverent treatment of the genre. The segment with the radio talk show conversations is sidesplitting; frequently the callers’ questions are ignored and instead they’re ridiculed by Ax and his hilariously psychotic father. And Axel’s ideas on the origin of the zombies and their intentions are absurdly funny. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer944246129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16278068803146360569">Guaranteed fun! If you like zombies and you love to laugh, this book’s for you. Especially if you get a warm tingly feeling every time a zombie gets put in its place.<br/> <br/>The details make this book go, and it flies! It was nonstop hilarious—much better than most other books in this genre. Readers who love to laugh will enjoy the very real personalities of the living, breathing characters and their earthiness, which makes for cheeky and hysterical dialogue. Most refreshing—and thought provoking—was t</span>
  <span id="freeText16278068803146360569" style="display:none">Guaranteed fun! If you like zombies and you love to laugh, this book’s for you. Especially if you get a warm tingly feeling every time a zombie gets put in its place.<br /> <br />The details make this book go, and it flies! It was nonstop hilarious—much better than most other books in this genre. Readers who love to laugh will enjoy the very real personalities of the living, breathing characters and their earthiness, which makes for cheeky and hysterical dialogue. Most refreshing—and thought provoking—was their often dangerously casual indifference toward the zombies. I was intrigued by the fascinating main character's frequent nonchalance regarding the zombie menace, and I was continuously surprised by his sudden comical outbursts and antics; nothing is out of bounds when it comes to the way Ax Handel treats the irrepressible zombies.<br /> <br />I can’t remember the last time I laughed so much. It made me wish I lived next door to the dysfunctional Handel family so that I might get a closer glimpse at what goes on over there. Hope there's a sequel!<br /> </span>

<div id="review_982691721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/982691721" />
    <a title="Sara Glickson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32351689-sara-glickson"><img alt="Sara Glickson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404159971p2/32351689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/982691721?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Glickson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Glickson" href="/user/show/32351689-sara-glickson">Sara Glickson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982691721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13288539862114855427">Smith has created something new and different here, and it’s absolutely hilarious. <br/><br/>His main character, Ax Handel, is an oddball independent thinker with an unflappable burnt-out mother, a spaced-out father, and a spiteful girlfriend from hell. And that's not all. One day he finds he’s got zombies running amok in his yard. That would be enough to make anyone run for the hills, but Ax is not a quitter, and while most people would view his situation as hopeless and dangerous, he sees opportunity. <br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText13288539862114855427" style="display:none">Smith has created something new and different here, and it’s absolutely hilarious. <br /><br />His main character, Ax Handel, is an oddball independent thinker with an unflappable burnt-out mother, a spaced-out father, and a spiteful girlfriend from hell. And that's not all. One day he finds he’s got zombies running amok in his yard. That would be enough to make anyone run for the hills, but Ax is not a quitter, and while most people would view his situation as hopeless and dangerous, he sees opportunity. <br /><br />I love the way Ax Handel narrates the story: outrageously down to earth. He's the kind of guy you want for your best friend, but every once in a while you want to flip open that little door on the back of his head to check inside and see if some of the wires aren't crossed. This book is Dave Barry funny.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13288539862114855427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17257267772615153365">Donnie Smith's "We Got Zombies on the Lawn Again, Ma," is a chuckle out loud read. Donnie's writing is very train of thought as his main character Ax Handel describes his personal tribulations dealing with crazy family members, a weird girlfriend, living in a small town... oh and zombies, there's those too.<br/><br/>I greatly appreciated that the character's voices remained consistent and realistic throughout the book, having spent years working with teenagers, this book often made me reminiscent of some </span>
  <span id="freeText17257267772615153365" style="display:none">Donnie Smith's "We Got Zombies on the Lawn Again, Ma," is a chuckle out loud read. Donnie's writing is very train of thought as his main character Ax Handel describes his personal tribulations dealing with crazy family members, a weird girlfriend, living in a small town... oh and zombies, there's those too.<br /><br />I greatly appreciated that the character's voices remained consistent and realistic throughout the book, having spent years working with teenagers, this book often made me reminiscent of some of the things I've heard them say. This book is chock full of puns, witty one-liners and awesome dialogue snippets. One of my favorites being:<br /><br />"You hit like a girl."<br /><br />"Well if you tried harder you could too!"<br /><br />Overall this was a fun and easy read. Fans of 'The Walking Dead,' 'Trailer Park Boys' and 'Reno 911' will love this book. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1729606059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729606059" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30337728-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558247206p2/30337728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729606059?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/30337728-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729606059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15021246704330624568"><b>Reading the List of Weird Book Titles is actually better than reading the books themselves.</b><br/><br/>So I'm really, really bored one day. I got the day off work and my choice of things to do are: watch the bat crap on the driveway get dry, reconcile my credit card statement or, look up lists of humorous book titles on Goodreads. I chose the later.<br/><br/>Have you ever looked at lists of funny book titles? There are some choice ones out there. In fact, I found a few I might even be slightly interested in reading (</span>
  <span id="freeText15021246704330624568" style="display:none"><b>Reading the List of Weird Book Titles is actually better than reading the books themselves.</b><br /><br />So I'm really, really bored one day. I got the day off work and my choice of things to do are: watch the bat crap on the driveway get dry, reconcile my credit card statement or, look up lists of humorous book titles on Goodreads. I chose the later.<br /><br />Have you ever looked at lists of funny book titles? There are some choice ones out there. In fact, I found a few I might even be slightly interested in reading (well anything's better than watching bat crap dry). Some of my choices were: Ass Goblins of Auschwitz, Stop Dressing Your Six Year Old Like a Skank, The Big Book of Lesbian Horse Stories, Robocunt and the Rug Niggers of Afrofaggotstan (yes these are real titles), and of course, the one I chose, We Got Zombies on the Lawn Again Ma.<br /><br />Donnie Smith writes of Ax Handel and his ma, aptly named Ma (presumably short for Ma Chette - see what I did there). Ax is a 19 year old pizza delivery guy with anger management issues and a yard full of zombies. Donnie's writing style is - well - not really a style so much, as writing down the first funny thing that comes into his head, and then writing down the next...and the next and so on. There were lots of humorous one (or two) liners mixed in there as it turns out, and that's the only reason I finished the book. I shall steal them and use them in everyday conversation from this day forth. Folks, this is NOT a literary masterpiece; this is redneck humor for the weak-minded, like me I suppose...but in my defence, I was pretty bored. <br /><br />I guess when you look at lists of weird book titles, don't expect the books to be any good. Although Dr Seuss did write, "There's a Wocket in my Pocket" which I will study studiously during my next boredom sesh. Hmm. I wonder if that bat crap on our driveway is dry yet? I better go check.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15021246704330624568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1337229488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1337229488" />
    <a title="Nathan Hillyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18913528-nathan-hillyer"><img alt="Nathan Hillyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366550512p2/18913528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337229488?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan Hillyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan Hillyer" href="/user/show/18913528-nathan-hillyer">Nathan Hillyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18913528-nathan-hillyer?shelf=awful">awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337229488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12854860457823632987">My tattoo artist recently laughed at me when I was telling him about another book I was reading, Inside the Outbreaks about Epidemic Intelligence Service. He said, "You always come in here reading some book, but it is never the same type of book. But you read that book (about the EIS), and in the same breath tell me you are reading a book called We Got Zombies On the Lawn Again, Ma. What possessed you to read that?!" I tend to read about 3 books concurrently, and I read books of all kinds, so wh</span>
  <span id="freeText12854860457823632987" style="display:none">My tattoo artist recently laughed at me when I was telling him about another book I was reading, Inside the Outbreaks about Epidemic Intelligence Service. He said, "You always come in here reading some book, but it is never the same type of book. But you read that book (about the EIS), and in the same breath tell me you are reading a book called We Got Zombies On the Lawn Again, Ma. What possessed you to read that?!" I tend to read about 3 books concurrently, and I read books of all kinds, so why not? <br /><br />This is the first single star review I have ever done. Most people ignore 1 star reviews, I think, because they feel it is just too low and biased by personality. So, I have to assume that probably if you are reading this, you already know why I gave it a single star review because you know now in retrospect. I think the reason I felt that I had to was that I recently gave Neuromancer a 2 star review for various reasons of personal irritation with the style, lack of weight in the conflict, and then a resolution I just didn't even care about by the end. But here is the thing: it HAD a plot. It had exposition, complication, climax, and a resolution. This book does not. The excuse is that it is a rambling notebook diary format from the point of view of an uneducated 19 year old pizza delivery guy named Ax Handel who just writes the way he thinks. Yup, he rambles. About the same kind of thing over and over and over - which is mostly about anything other than zombies and mostly metaphors about being a tough guy. In his ongoing internal monologue, it is like a stand up comedian constantly going off in different directions and "Have you ever noticed?" scenarios. There are characters, yes, on the periphery, and all of them seem to talk the same way he does. They all bait and switch each other randomly like a vaudevillian dialog sequence between Groucho and Chico Marx, except that stops being funny after the first time it is done. (By the way, the Marx Brothers were framed by stories and were much more skilled in their banter. For the record, I love the Marx Brothers.) In the beginning, we are introduced to his ex-girlfriend, and we think here is the romantic interest. She is interesting and would be a good source of conflict and eventual resolution, and she disappears immediately. Then there is his tough mother and his ex-con father. (Everyone is tough in this book, and the men often bait anyone else into an implication they that they are gay, which is repetitive enough to be homophobic.) Those are the characters, and they occasionally provide a source of back and forth Abbot and Costello type confused misdirection to the point of becoming tedious. <br /><br />And the zombies? Where are the zombies? Well, the first actual zombie encounter in which an incident with a zombie is involved occurs over 30% into the book. I thought, "OK, here is where the story finally starts!" No. We never find out why there are zombies, nor why anyone should care, and apart from beating them viciously in attempts to be funny, he doesn't do anything to eradicate them or even use them. The zombies are never more than just kind of irritating. They are just there sometimes. Only 4 times in the book, actually, and the second encounter with zombies is over 50% into the book. There are two more zombie scenes, and the most interesting and promising part of the book involves a talking zombie dog, and two zombie mobsters. It was almost enjoyable, but they never recur. I even had a dwindling hope that they would. Nope. The last 12 - 15% of the book was all a call-in radio program he does with his father involving people threatening each other, suggesting the callers are gay, and fighting. So, maybe this book was the equivalent of a Jerry Springer show - with zombies in the background. <br /><br />This book has made me finally resolved to go back to reading sample chapters first and stop buying books with what seems like a promising or amusing scenario blogs. So, why the hell did I read all the way to the end. Well, I paid for the book as I said. It may be that I felt compelled to give it every last chance I could to find positive elements. It did sometimes make me grin. I realize now that it may be the worst book I have ever read because I can't quite think of anything worse. I used to think it was The Bourne Identity or Inferno (Dan Brown, not Dante) or Never Let Me Go by Kazuo Ishiguro. I pretty much hated all 3 of those books, but despite being facile, two-dimensional, or stylistically nauseous, those books had actual stories. There are plenty of the worst books I have NEVER read, like anything by Ayn Rand because I disagree completely with her philosophy, but this one I read. All the way to the end, and that is important because I was sure of the reason I gave it one star. Sorry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12854860457823632987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601109564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1632031725130763192">We Got Zombies in the Lawn Again, Ma is a hilarious tale of Ax Handel and his experience with zombies. Although a little slow to start with the first few chapters describing the writing style; the book then turns into a hilarious story of Axel and his mom battling zombies there first few nights at a new home. The story introduces characters whom seem so interesting that the reader wants to see more of them. The book ends with a humorous “call line” in which Axel and his father attempt to answer </span>
  <span id="freeText1632031725130763192" style="display:none">We Got Zombies in the Lawn Again, Ma is a hilarious tale of Ax Handel and his experience with zombies. Although a little slow to start with the first few chapters describing the writing style; the book then turns into a hilarious story of Axel and his mom battling zombies there first few nights at a new home. The story introduces characters whom seem so interesting that the reader wants to see more of them. The book ends with a humorous “call line” in which Axel and his father attempt to answer zombie questions which only leads to more of their off track conversations which relates back to Axel as a character as a whole in which half the time makes no sense when he talks. All in all, the character of Axel Handel makes the book a good read just to see where his ever traveling mind goes. </span>

  <span id="freeText10675855309766959815" style="display:none">I'm usually immune to "funny" books so it's properly high praise when I say that this made me laugh out loud twice.<br />As Homer Simpson would say, this is "just a bunch of stuff that happened" meaning it's not so much a novel with a plot as a collection of comedy anecdotes about Ax beating up the zombies. Which might be why I actually didn't find the zombie parts as interesting as Ax's perceptions of and interactions with the world around him. But if you approach it that way and read it a little bit at a time it's better and more entertaining because otherwise the manic pace of the prose gets sort of draining and hard to concentrate on. Then again, that could be a personal thing because as I said, issues with funny books.<br />The cover doesn't have any branding, it looks self-published? Well done, Smith!<br /><br /> </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a3T/5/ttXl9mCncL8qL4/0KkFV6Dthf4BunYIkLSGixRUpY1QDOXN8Ehw2oFV/IglPvylk07mZ9dl56Tj5Hotg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4426187176652313738">Donnie Smith is a former writing teacher with degrees in education and history from the University of North Dakota who recently published his first book, We Got Zombies On The Lawn Again, Ma (CreateSpace, November 2013). It's the first in his three-book series, a humorously irreverent take on zombies starring the indomitable Ax Handel. Donnie began as a storyteller by swapping dark and funny tales</span>
  <span id="freeText4426187176652313738" style="display:none">Donnie Smith is a former writing teacher with degrees in education and history from the University of North Dakota who recently published his first book, We Got Zombies On The Lawn Again, Ma (CreateSpace, November 2013). It's the first in his three-book series, a humorously irreverent take on zombies starring the indomitable Ax Handel. Donnie began as a storyteller by swapping dark and funny tales with inmates in the facility where he worked as a correctional officer over twenty years ago, and today utilizes versions of those stories in his writing. </span>
